## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of concentration change dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics. Rate laws of various orders, autocatalytic mechanisms, and reversible reactions all produce characteristic functional forms relating dA/dt to A.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction kinetics)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (generalized rate law with source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding/reaction)
- Parallel pathway: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 + c3 (multiple simultaneous reaction channels)
- Damped time-modulated rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * t) (linearly time-varying rate coefficient)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure power-law dependence on concentration (dA/dt ~ A^n) indicates an elementary reaction of order n
- A linear relationship dA/dt vs A with nonzero intercept suggests a reversible reaction or constant source/sink term
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(K+A)) indicate saturation or enzyme-mediated catalysis where substrate binding limits the rate
- Product form A*(C-A) indicates autocatalytic behavior where the product catalyzes its own formation from a fixed total pool
- Explicit time dependence in the rate law suggests non-isothermal conditions, photochemical forcing, or catalyst deactivation
- Square of a rational function (A/(K+A))^2 or denominator (1+A)^2 suggests competitive inhibition or bimolecular surface mechanisms
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A indicates parallel or competing reaction pathways
- Negative sign convention: dA/dt is typically negative for reactant consumption, so the leading coefficient c0 is expected to be negative when A is a reactant
